			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0"><p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<p><b>PayPal Holdings, Inc.</b> is an American company operating a worldwide online payments system that supports <a href="/wiki/E-commerce_payment_system" title="E-commerce payment system">online money transfers</a> and serves as an electronic alternative to traditional <a href="/wiki/Banknote" title="Banknote">paper</a> methods like <a href="/wiki/Cheque" title="Cheque">checks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Money_order" title="Money order">money orders</a>. The company operates as a payment processor for online vendors, <a href="/wiki/Auction" title="Auction">auction</a> sites, and many other commercial users, for which it charges a fee in exchange for benefits such as one-click transactions and password memory.

decoding="async" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> 305 million (2019)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Launched</th><td>December 1998<span style="display:none"> (<span class="bday dtstart published updated">1998-12</span>)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Current status</th><td class="category">Active</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Computing_platform" title="Computing platform">Native client(s) on</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a><br><a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a><br><a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Windows</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Written in</th><td><a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B" title="C++">C++</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a> (as <a href="/wiki/Node.js" title="Node.js">Node.js</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Python_(programming_language)" title="Python (programming language)">Python</a><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PayPal_San_Jose_Headquarters.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/PayPal_San_Jose_Headquarters.jpg/220px-PayPal_San_Jose_Headquarters.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PayPal_San_Jose_Headquarters.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>PayPal's corporate headquarters in <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">San Jose, California</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EBayTorontoOffice2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/EBayTorontoOffice2.JPG/170px-EBayTorontoOffice2.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="257" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="4928"></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EBayTorontoOffice2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/EBay" title="EBay">eBay</a>, PayPal, <a href="/wiki/Kijiji" title="Kijiji">Kijiji</a> and <a href="/wiki/StubHub" title="StubHub">StubHub</a> in Toronto</div></div></div>
<p>Established in 1998 as Confinity,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> PayPal had its <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> in 2002, and became a wholly owned subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/EBay" title="EBay">eBay</a> later that year.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nytimes02_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes02-12">[12]</a></sup>  eBay <a href="/wiki/Corporate_spin-off" title="Corporate spin-off">spun off</a> PayPal in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters2014_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters2014-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sec_gov_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sec_gov-5">[5]</a></sup>
The company ranked 204th on the 2019 <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> of the largest United States corporations by revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-Fortune_500_Companies_2018_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fortune_500_Companies_2018-14">[14]</a></sup></p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_PayPal" title="Timeline of PayPal">Timeline of PayPal</a></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early history" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>PayPal was originally established by <a href="/wiki/Max_Levchin" title="Max Levchin">Max Levchin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Thiel" title="Peter Thiel">Peter Thiel</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Luke_Nosek" title="Luke Nosek">Luke Nosek</a> in December 1998 as <a href="/wiki/Confinity" title="Confinity">Confinity</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-techrepublic_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-techrepublic-15">[15]</a></sup> a company that developed security software for handheld devices.<sup id="cite_ref-entrepreneur_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-entrepreneur-16">[16]</a></sup></p><p>In March 2000, Confinity merged with <a href="/wiki/X.com" title="X.com">X.com</a>, an online banking company founded by <a href="/wiki/Elon_Musk" title="Elon Musk">Elon Musk</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fastco2012_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fastco2012-17">[17]</a></sup> Musk was optimistic about the future success of the money transfer business Confinity was developing.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Musk and Bill Harris, then-president and CEO of X.com, disagreed about the potential future success of the money transfer business and Harris left the company in May 2000.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In October of that year, Musk decided that X.com would terminate its other internet banking operations and focus on PayPal.<sup id="cite_ref-Startup_Playbook_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Startup_Playbook-18">[18]</a></sup> That same month, Elon Musk was replaced by Peter Thiel as CEO of X.com,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> which was renamed PayPal in 2001 and went <a href="/wiki/IPO" class="mw-redirect" title="IPO">public</a> in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-bizfounders_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bizfounders-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Paypal's <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">IPO</a> listed under the ticker PYPL at $13 per share and generated over $61 million.<sup id="cite_ref-ecommerce02_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ecommerce02-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="eBay_subsidiary_.282002.E2.80.932014.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="eBay_subsidiary_(2002–2014)">eBay subsidiary (2002–2014)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: eBay subsidiary (2002–2014)" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Shortly after PayPal's <a href="/wiki/IPO" class="mw-redirect" title="IPO">IPO</a>, the company was acquired by <a href="/wiki/EBay" title="EBay">eBay</a> on October 3, 2002,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> for $1.5 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-Startup_Playbook_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Startup_Playbook-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fastcompany2014_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fastcompany2014-26">[26]</a></sup> More than 70 percent of all eBay auctions accepted PayPal payments, and roughly 1 in 4 closed auction listings were transacted via PayPal.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> PayPal became the default payment method used by the majority of eBay users, and the service competed with eBay's subsidiary <a href="/wiki/Billpoint" title="Billpoint">Billpoint</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Citibank" title="Citibank">Citibank</a>'s c2it, <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!" title="Yahoo!">Yahoo!</a>'s <a href="/wiki/PayDirect" title="PayDirect">PayDirect</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Google_Checkout" title="Google Checkout">Google Checkout</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>In 2005, PayPal acquired the <a href="/wiki/VeriSign" class="mw-redirect" title="VeriSign">VeriSign</a> payment solution to provide added security support.<sup id="cite_ref-ecommerce05_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ecommerce05-28">[28]</a></sup> In 2007, PayPal announced a partnership with <a href="/wiki/MasterCard" class="mw-redirect" title="MasterCard">MasterCard</a>, which led to the development and launch of the PayPal Secure Card service, a software that allows customers to make payments on websites that do not accept PayPal directly.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters2007_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters2007-29">[29]</a></sup> By the end of 2007, the company generated $1.8 billion in revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-cnnmoney_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnnmoney-30">[30]</a></sup></p><p>In January 2008, PayPal acquired Fraud Sciences, a privately held Israeli start-up that developed online risk tools, for $169 million.<sup id="cite_ref-techcrunchha_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-techcrunchha-31">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> In November 2008, the company acquired <a href="/wiki/Bill_Me_Later" class="mw-redirect" title="Bill Me Later">Bill Me Later</a>, an online transactional credit company.<sup id="cite_ref-incmag08_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-incmag08-33">[33]</a></sup></p><p>By 2010, PayPal had over 100 million active user accounts in 190 markets through 25 different currencies.<sup id="cite_ref-galeecommerce_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-galeecommerce-34">[34]</a></sup> In July 2011, fourteen alleged members of the <a href="/wiki/Anonymous_(group)" title="Anonymous (group)">Anonymous</a> <a href="/wiki/Hacktivist" class="mw-redirect" title="Hacktivist">hacktivist</a> group were charged with attempting to disrupt PayPal's operations. The <a href="/wiki/Denial_of_service" class="mw-redirect" title="Denial of service">denial of service</a> attacks occurred in December 2010, after PayPal stopped processing donations to <a href="/wiki/WikiLeaks" title="WikiLeaks">WikiLeaks</a>. On December 5, 2013, 13 of the <a href="/wiki/PayPal_14" title="PayPal 14">PayPal 14</a> pleaded guilty to misdemeanor and felony charges related to the attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-David_Gilbert_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-David_Gilbert-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steven_Musil_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steven_Musil-36">[36]</a></sup></p><p>The company continued to build its Merchant Services division, providing <a href="/wiki/E-payment" class="mw-redirect" title="E-payment">e-payments</a> for retailers on eBay. In 2011, PayPal announced that it would begin moving its business offline so that customers can make payments via PayPal in stores.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> In August 2012, the company announced its partnership with <a href="/wiki/Discover_Card" title="Discover Card">Discover Card</a> to allow PayPal payments to be made at any of the 7 million stores in Discover Card's network.<sup id="cite_ref-forbesbarth_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbesbarth-38">[38]</a></sup> By the end of 2012, PayPal's total payment volume processed was <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>145,000,000,000.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> and accounted for 40% of eBay's revenue, amounting to <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>1,370,000,000 in the 3rd quarter of 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-samuels2012_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-samuels2012-40">[40]</a></sup></p><p>In 2013, PayPal acquired IronPearl, a <a href="/wiki/Palo_Alto" class="mw-redirect" title="Palo Alto">Palo Alto</a> startup offering engagement software,<sup id="cite_ref-venturebeat2013_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-venturebeat2013-41">[41]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Braintree_(company)" title="Braintree (company)">Braintree</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Payment_gateway" title="Payment gateway">payment gateway</a>, to further product development and mobile services.<sup id="cite_ref-techcrunchrao_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-techcrunchrao-42">[42]</a></sup> In June 2014 <a href="/wiki/David_A._Marcus" title="David A. Marcus">David Marcus</a> announced he was leaving his role<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> as PayPal President; Marcus joined PayPal in August 2011 after its acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Zong_mobile_payments" title="Zong mobile payments">Zong</a>, of which he was the founder and CEO.<sup id="cite_ref-duryee2012_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-duryee2012-44">[44]</a></sup> David Marcus succeeded <a href="/wiki/Scott_Thompson_(businessman)" title="Scott Thompson (businessman)">Scott Thompson</a> as president, who left the role to join <a href="/wiki/Yahoo" class="mw-redirect" title="Yahoo">Yahoo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-duryee2012_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-duryee2012-44">[44]</a></sup> PayPal announced that Marcus would be succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Dan_Schulman" title="Dan Schulman">Dan Schulman</a>, who previously served as CEO of <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Mobile" title="Virgin Mobile">Virgin Mobile</a> and Executive vice president of <a href="/wiki/American_Express" title="American Express">American Express</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bizjournal2014_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bizjournal2014-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Spin-off_from_eBay_.282014.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Spin-off_from_eBay_(2014–present)">Spin-off from eBay (2014–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Spin-off from eBay (2014–present)" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>It was announced on September 30, 2014, that eBay would spin off PayPal into a separate publicly traded company, a move demanded in 2013 by activist hedge fund magnate <a href="/wiki/Carl_Icahn" title="Carl Icahn">Carl Icahn</a>. The spin-off was completed on July 18, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dan_Schulman" title="Dan Schulman">Dan Schulman</a> is the current President and CEO, with former eBay CEO <a href="/wiki/John_Donahoe" title="John Donahoe">John Donahoe</a> serving as chairman.<sup id="cite_ref-bizjournal2014_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bizjournal2014-45">[45]</a></sup> On Jan 31, 2018 eBay announced that, "After the existing eBay-PayPal agreement ends in 2020, PayPal will remain a payment option for shoppers on eBay, but it won’t be prominently featured ahead of debit and credit card options as it is today. PayPal will cease to process card payments for eBay at that time." <sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p><p>On July 1, 2015, PayPal announced that it was acquiring digital money transfer company <a href="/wiki/Xoom_Corporation" title="Xoom Corporation">Xoom Corporation</a>. PayPal spent $25 a share in cash to acquire the publicly traded Xoom, or about $1.09 billion. The deal was closed in the fourth quarter of 2015. The move strengthened PayPal’s international business, giving it access to Xoom’s 1.3 million active U.S. customers that sent about $7 billion in the 12 months ending on March 31, to people in 37 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p><p>On September 1, 2015, PayPal launched their <a href="/wiki/Peer-to-peer" title="Peer-to-peer">peer-to-peer</a> payment platform "PayPal.Me", a service that allows users to send a custom link to request funds via text, email, or other messaging platforms.<sup id="cite_ref-PayPalMeTechCrunch_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PayPalMeTechCrunch-53">[53]</a></sup> Custom links are set to be structured as PayPal.me/username/amountrequested.<sup id="cite_ref-PayPalMeTechCrunch_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PayPalMeTechCrunch-53">[53]</a></sup>  PayPal.Me was launched in 18 countries including <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PayPalMeEngadget_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PayPalMeEngadget-54">[54]</a></sup> PayPal had 170 million users, as of September 2015, and the focus of PayPal.Me was to create a mobile-first user experience that enables faster payment sharing than PayPal's traditional tools.<sup id="cite_ref-PayPalMeTechCrunch_53-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PayPalMeTechCrunch-53">[53]</a></sup></p><p>On May 17, 2018, PayPal agreed to purchase Swedish payment processor <a href="/wiki/IZettle" title="IZettle">iZettle</a> for $2.2 billion. This is PayPal's largest acquisition to date and the company claims that it is the in-store expertise and digital marketing strength that will complement its own online and mobile payment services.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-55">[55]</a></sup></p><p>On March 19, 2019, PayPal announced their partnership with <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a> as part of the company's new checkout feature, "Checkout on Instagram".<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p><p>In June 2019, PayPal reported that Chief Operating Officer Bill Ready would be leaving the company at the end of the year. In December 2019, Google announced that Ready would become the new commerce chief.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>

<td><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">Finances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Finances" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<p>For the fiscal year 2017, PayPal reported earnings of US$1.795 billion, with an annual revenue of $13.094 billion, an increase of 20.8% over the previous fiscal cycle. PayPal's shares traded at over $55 per share, and its market capitalization was valued at over $98.2 billion in October 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
