</td></tr></tbody></table></section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Offices">Offices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Offices" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PayPal_Headquarters.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/PayPal_Headquarters.jpg/220px-PayPal_Headquarters.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="400"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 176px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/PayPal_Headquarters.jpg/220px-PayPal_Headquarters.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="176" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PayPal_Headquarters.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>PayPal Operations Center and main office in <a href="/wiki/Omaha,_Nebraska" title="Omaha, Nebraska">Omaha, Nebraska</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>PayPal's corporate headquarters are located in the <a href="/wiki/North_San_Jose_Innovation_District" title="North San Jose Innovation District">North San Jose Innovation District</a> of <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">San Jose, California</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-samuels2012_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-samuels2012-40">[40]</a></sup> at North First Street campus.<sup id="cite_ref-bizjournalsanjose_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bizjournalsanjose-85">[85]</a></sup> The company's operations center is located in <a href="/wiki/Omaha,_Nebraska" title="Omaha, Nebraska">Omaha, Nebraska</a>, which was opened in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-journalstar_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-journalstar-86">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Virgil_Larson_2007_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Virgil_Larson_2007-87">[87]</a></sup> Since July 2007, PayPal has operated across the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> as a Luxembourg-based bank. The PayPal European headquarters are located in <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a> and the international headquarters are in <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>. PayPal opened a technology center in <a href="/wiki/Scottsdale,_Arizona" title="Scottsdale, Arizona">Scottsdale, Arizona</a> in 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-auctionbytes.com_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auctionbytes.com-88">[88]</a></sup> and a software development center in <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a>, India in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> In October 2007, PayPal opened a data service office on the north side of <a href="/wiki/Austin,_Texas" title="Austin, Texas">Austin, Texas</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-bizjournalatx_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bizjournalatx-90">[90]</a></sup> and also opened a second operations center in <a href="/wiki/La_Vista,_Nebraska" title="La Vista, Nebraska">La Vista, Nebraska</a> that same year.<sup id="cite_ref-journalstar_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-journalstar-86">[86]</a></sup> In 2011, joining similar customer support operations located in <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, Germany; <a href="/wiki/Chandler,_Arizona" title="Chandler, Arizona">Chandler, Arizona</a>; <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dundalk" title="Dundalk">Dundalk</a>, Ireland; <a href="/wiki/Omaha,_Nebraska" title="Omaha, Nebraska">Omaha, Nebraska</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>, China; PayPal opened a second customer support center in <a href="/wiki/Kuala_Lumpur" title="Kuala Lumpur">Kuala Lumpur</a>, Malaysia, and began the hiring process.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> In 2014, PayPal opened a new global center of operations in Kuala Lumpur.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Services" data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<p>As of 2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, PayPal operates in 202 markets and has 305 million active, registered accounts. PayPal allows customers to send, receive, and hold funds in 25 currencies worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p><p>PayPal's services allow people to make <a href="/wiki/Financial_transaction" title="Financial transaction">financial transactions</a> online by granting the ability to <a href="/wiki/Electronic_funds_transfer" title="Electronic funds transfer">transfer funds electronically</a> between individuals and businesses.<sup id="cite_ref-howitworks_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-howitworks-94">[94]</a></sup> Through PayPal, users can send or receive payments for online auctions on websites like eBay, purchase or sell goods and services, or donate money or receive donations. It is not necessary to have a PayPal account to use the company's services.<sup id="cite_ref-howitworks_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-howitworks-94">[94]</a></sup> PayPal account users can set currency conversion option in account settings.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p><p>From 2009 to 2016, PayPal operated Student Accounts, allowing parents to set up a student account, transfer money into it, and obtain a debit card for student use. The program provided tools to teach how to spend money wisely and take responsibility for actions.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nybits_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nybits-97">[97]</a></sup>  PayPal discontinued Student Accounts in August 2016.
</p><p>In November 2009, PayPal opened its platform, allowing other services to get access to its code and to use its infrastructure in order to enable peer-to-peer online transactions.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p><p>In 2007, PayPal acquired the online credit product Bill Me Later, Inc., which has since been rebranded as PayPal Credit and provided services for Comenity Capital Bank, the lender of PayPal Credit accounts.  Founded in 2000, Bill Me Later is headquartered in Timonium, Maryland, with additional offices in Hunt Valley, Maryland; Chandler, Arizona; and San Francisco, California.  PayPal Credit offers shoppers access to an instant online revolving line of credit at thousands of vendors that accept PayPal, subject to credit approval.  PayPal Credit allows consumers to shop online in much the same way as they would with a traditional credit card.  The rebranding of Bill Me Later as PayPal Credit also means that consumers can use PayPal Credit to fund transactions virtually anywhere PayPal is accepted.<sup id="cite_ref-billmelater.com_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billmelater.com-99">[99]</a></sup> In 2015 PayPal agreed that PayPal Credit would pay a $25 million fine to settle a complaint filed in Federal Court by the <a href="/wiki/Consumer_Financial_Protection_Bureau" title="Consumer Financial Protection Bureau">Consumer Financial Protection Bureau</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cfpb_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfpb-100">[100]</a></sup></p><p>The PayPal app is available online or at the <a href="/wiki/ITunes_App_Store" class="mw-redirect" title="ITunes App Store">iTunes App Store</a> and <a href="/wiki/Google_Play" title="Google Play">Google Play</a>.  One year after acquiring <a href="/wiki/Braintree_(company)" title="Braintree (company)">Braintree</a>, PayPal introduced its "One Touch" service, which allows users to pay with a one-touch option on participating merchants websites or apps.<sup id="cite_ref-recode2014_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recode2014-101">[101]</a></sup></p><p>On November 28, 2011, PayPal reported <a href="/wiki/Black_Friday_(shopping)" title="Black Friday (shopping)">Black Friday</a> brought record mobile engagement including a 538% increase in global mobile payment volume when compared with Black Friday 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-post1_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-post1-102">[102]</a></sup></p><p>In 2012, the company launched "PayPal Here", a small business mobile payment system that includes a combination of a free <a href="/wiki/Mobile_app" title="Mobile app">mobile app</a> and a small card-reader that plugs into a smart phone.<sup id="cite_ref-mashable2012_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mashable2012-103">[103]</a></sup></p><p>PayPal launched an updated app for <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> and <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> in 2013 that expanded its mobile app capabilities by allowing users to search for local shops and restaurants that accept PayPal payments, order ahead at participating venues, and access their PayPal Credit accounts (formerly known as Bill Me Later).<sup id="cite_ref-billmelater.com_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billmelater.com-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_model_evolution">Business model evolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Business model evolution" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>PayPal's success in users and volumes was the product of a three-phase strategy described by former eBay CEO <a href="/wiki/Meg_Whitman" title="Meg Whitman">Meg Whitman</a>: "First, PayPal focused on expanding its service among eBay users in the US. Second, we began expanding PayPal to eBay's international sites. And third, we started to build PayPal's business off eBay."<sup id="cite_ref-wallstfolly_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wallstfolly-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Phase_1">Phase 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Phase 1" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In the first phase, payment volumes were coming mostly from the eBay auction website. The system was very attractive to auction sellers, most of which were individuals or small businesses that were unable to accept credit cards, and for consumers as well.
In fact, many sellers could not qualify for a credit card Merchant account because they lacked a commercial credit history. The service also appealed to auction buyers because they could fund PayPal accounts using credit cards or bank account balances, without divulging credit card numbers to unknown sellers. PayPal employed an aggressive marketing campaign to accelerate its growth, depositing $10 in new users' PayPal accounts.<sup id="cite_ref-wallstfolly_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wallstfolly-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Phase_2">Phase 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Phase 2" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Until 2000, PayPal's strategy was to earn interest on funds in PayPal accounts. However, most recipients of PayPal credits withdrew funds immediately. Also, a large majority of senders funded their payments using credit cards, which cost PayPal roughly 2% of payment value per transaction.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>To solve this problem, PayPal tailored its product to cater more to business accounts. Instead of relying on interests earned from deposited funds, PayPal started relying on earnings from service charges. They offered seller protection to PayPal account holders, provided that they comply with reimbursement policies. For example, PayPal merchants are either required to retain a traceable proof of shipping to a confirmed address or to provide a signed receipt for items valued over $750.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Phase_3">Phase 3</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Phase 3" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>After fine-tuning PayPal's business model and increasing its domestic and international penetration on eBay, PayPal started its off-eBay strategy. This was based on developing stronger growth in active users by adding users across multiple platforms, despite the slowdown in on-eBay growth and low-single-digit user growth on the eBay site. A late 2003 reorganization created a new business unit within PayPal—Merchant Services—to provide payment solutions to small and large e-commerce merchants outside the eBay auction community. Starting in the second half of 2004, PayPal Merchant Services unveiled several initiatives to enroll online merchants outside the eBay auction community, including:<sup id="cite_ref-wallstfolly_104-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wallstfolly-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li>Lowering its transaction fee for high-volume merchants from 2.2% to 1.9% (while increasing the monthly transaction volume required to qualify for the lowest fee to $100,000)</li>
<li>Encouraging its users to recruit non-eBay merchants by increasing its referral bonus to a maximum of $1,000 (versus the previous $100 cap)</li>
<li>Persuading credit card gateway providers, including CyberSource and Retail Decisions USA, to include PayPal among their offerings to online merchants.</li>
<li>Hiring a new sales force to acquire large merchants such as Dell, Apple's iTunes, and Yahoo! Stores, which hosted thousands of online merchants</li>
<li>Reducing fees for online music purchases and other "micropayments"</li>
<li>Launching PayPal Mobile, which allowed users to make payments using text messaging on their cell phones</li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_reach">Global reach</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Global reach" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>PayPal can be used in more than 200 countries/regions.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p><p>Different countries have different conditions: <i>Send only</i> (Package Service allows sending only, valid in 97 countries), <i>PayPal Zero</i> (package suggests the possibility of enrollment, entry, and withdrawal of funds in foreign currency, but the user can not hold the balance PayPal account, operates in 18 countries), <i>SRW Send - Receive - Withdrawal</i> (the possibility of enrollment, input-output and the ability to keep your PayPal account balance in the currency and to transfer to the card when the user sees fit, operates in 41 countries) and <i>Local Currency</i> (SRW plus opportunity to conduct transactions in the local currency, 21 countries).
</p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: China" data-section="14" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In July 2017, PayPal announced a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Baidu" title="Baidu">Baidu</a>, to allow the Chinese firm’s 100 million mobile wallet users to make payments to PayPal’s 17 million merchants through the Baidu service.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Crimea">Crimea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Crimea" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In January 2015, PayPal ceased operations in <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">Crimea</a> in compliance with international sanctions against Russia and Crimea.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: India" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>As of March 2011, PayPal has made changes to the User Agreement for Indian users to comply with <a href="/wiki/Reserve_Bank_of_India" title="Reserve Bank of India">Reserve Bank of India</a> regulations.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> The per transaction limit had been set to USD $3,000, since October 14, 2011. However, on July 29, 2013, PayPal increased the per transaction limit to USD $10,000.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> This brings the per transaction limit for India in line with the restrictions imposed by PayPal in most other countries.
</p><p>PayPal has disabled sending and receiving personal payments in India, thus forcing all recipients to pay a transaction fee.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p><p>PayPal plans to make India an incubation center for the company's employee engagement policies. In 2012, PayPal hired 120 people for its offices in Chennai and Bangaluru.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p><p>On 8 November 2017, PayPal launched domestic operations under PayPal Payments Private Limited and now provides digital payment solutions for merchants and customers in India.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> As of 2020, Paypal supports the domestic card system <a href="/wiki/RuPay" title="RuPay">RuPay</a> and is planning to further integrate <a href="/wiki/Unified_Payments_Interface" title="Unified Payments Interface">Unified Payment Interface</a> (UPI) in collaboration with <a href="/wiki/National_Payments_Corporation_of_India" title="National Payments Corporation of India">National Payments Corporation of India</a> (NPCI).<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Paypal now has the largest global engineering team in India outside of US that is spread over <a href="/wiki/Bengaluru" class="mw-redirect" title="Bengaluru">Bengaluru</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Chennai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad" title="Hyderabad">Hyderabad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Israel_and_Palestinian_Territories">Israel and Palestinian Territories</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Israel and Palestinian Territories" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>PayPal is available in <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> but is not available in the <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_territories" title="Palestinian territories">Palestinian territories</a>. Nor can Palestinians working in the <a href="/wiki/West_Bank" title="West Bank">West Bank</a> or <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza</a> access it but Israelis living in <a href="/wiki/Israeli_settlement" title="Israeli settlement">settlements</a> in the West Bank can use PayPal. This discrepancy has prompted Palestinian tech companies to seek a policy change from PayPal.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">Japan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Japan" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In late March 2010, new Japanese banking regulations forced PayPal Japan to suspend the ability of personal account holders registered in Japan from sending or receiving money between individuals and as a result are now subject to PayPal's business fees on all transactions.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Pakistan">Pakistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Pakistan" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In Pakistan, users can use <a href="/wiki/Xoom_Corporation" title="Xoom Corporation">Xoom</a>, a money transfer service owned by PayPal.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> In October 2018, <a href="/wiki/Goverment_of_Pakistan" class="mw-redirect" title="Goverment of Pakistan">Pakistan's government</a> used Xoom to help crowdsource funds for the purpose of building two dams.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Turkey">Turkey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Turkey" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>Eight years after the company first started operating in the country, Paypal ceased operations in Turkey on 6 June 2016 when Turkish financial regulator BDDK denied it a payment license. The regulators had demanded that PayPal's data centers be located inside Turkey to facilitate compliance with government and court orders to block content and to generate tax revenue. PayPal said that the closure will affect tens of thousands of businesses and hundreds of thousands of consumers in Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Sri_Lanka">Sri Lanka</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sri Lanka" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In January 2017, PayPal team scheduled to visit <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> mid January to re-establish links.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="PayPal_Giving_Fund">PayPal Giving Fund</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: PayPal Giving Fund" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>PayPal Giving Fund is a registered charity supported by Paypal that streamlines donations to nonprofit organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Digital_marketing_with_PayPal">Digital marketing with PayPal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Digital marketing with PayPal" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<p>PayPal launches different marketing activities in various channels and emphasizes that consumers can use it in different ways.<sup id="cite_ref-jenni_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jenni-127">[127]</a></sup> Paypal's marketing includes the TV commercials, outdoor advertising, <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a>, and display advertisement.<sup id="cite_ref-jenni_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jenni-127">[127]</a></sup></p><p>PayPal provides free analytics to traders about the ways that consumers utilise <a href="/wiki/Online_payments" class="mw-redirect" title="Online payments">online payments</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gesen_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gesen-128">[128]</a></sup> By the free tracking service, PayPal assists traders to target the consumers. PayPal's code gathers the consumer information which can be installed on the trader's website.<sup id="cite_ref-gesen_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gesen-128">[128]</a></sup> Both PayPal and traders get benefit from the free service.
</p><p>PayPal cooperates with "Synchrony Financial" and provides a financial service to <a href="/wiki/Mastercard" title="Mastercard">PayPal Cashback Mastercard</a>, which offers 2% return cash to customers who are shopping online or on the physical stores by using PayPal.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> PayPal’s cashback financial service promotes the number of potential customers.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a> allows PayPal as a mode of payment for <a href="/wiki/App_Store_(iOS)" title="App Store (iOS)">App Store</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apple_Music" title="Apple Music">Apple Music</a>, <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Apple_Books" title="Apple Books">Apple Books</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-spencer_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spencer-130">[130]</a></sup> PayPal can increase usage by the platform of Apple. In addition, PayPal gets revenue from Apple services especially from App Store.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup>  Customers can use PayPal to purchase by connecting their PayPal payment system to Apple ID accounts.<sup id="cite_ref-spencer_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spencer-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(6)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Regulation">Regulation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Regulation" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-6 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-6">
<p>Thiel, a founder of PayPal, has stated that PayPal is not a bank because it does not engage in <a href="/wiki/Fractional-reserve_banking" title="Fractional-reserve banking">fractional-reserve banking</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ecorner_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ecorner-132">[132]</a></sup> Rather, PayPal's funds that have not been disbursed are kept in commercial interest-bearing checking accounts.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, PayPal is licensed as a <a href="/wiki/Money_transmitter" title="Money transmitter">money transmitter</a>, on a state-by-state basis.<sup id="cite_ref-Wolverton_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wolverton-134">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> But state laws vary, as do their definitions of banks, narrow banks, money services businesses, and money transmitters.  Although PayPal is not classified as a bank, the company is subject to some of the rules and regulations governing the financial industry including <a href="/wiki/Regulation_E" class="mw-redirect" title="Regulation E">Regulation E</a> consumer protections and the <a href="/wiki/USA_PATRIOT_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="USA PATRIOT Act">USA PATRIOT Act</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> The most analogous regulatory source of law for PayPal transactions comes from <a href="/wiki/Peer-to-peer_banking" title="Peer-to-peer banking">peer-to-peer</a> (P2P) payments using credit and <a href="/wiki/Debit_cards" class="mw-redirect" title="Debit cards">debit cards</a>. Ordinarily, a credit card transaction, specifically the relationship between the issuing bank and the cardholder, is governed by the <a href="/wiki/Truth_in_Lending_Act" title="Truth in Lending Act">Truth in Lending Act</a> (TILA) 15 U.S.C. §§ 1601-1667f as implemented by Regulation Z, 12 C.F.R. 226, (TILA/Z). TILA/Z requires specific procedures for billing errors, dispute resolution, and limits cardholder liability for unauthorized charges.<sup id="cite_ref-margaretjane_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-margaretjane-137">[137]</a></sup> Similarly, the legal relationship between a debit cardholder and the issuing bank is regulated by the <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Funds_Transfer_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Electronic Funds Transfer Act">Electronic Funds Transfer Act</a> (EFTA) 15 U.S.C. §§ 1693-1693r, as implemented by Regulation E, 12 C.F.R. 205, (EFTA/E). EFTA/E is directed at consumer protection and provides strict error resolution procedures. However, because PayPal is a <i>payment intermediary</i> and not otherwise regulated directly, TILA/Z and EFTA/E do not operate exactly as written once the credit/debit card transaction occurs via PayPal. Basically, unless a PayPal transaction is funded with a credit card, the consumer has no recourse in the event of fraud by the seller.<sup id="cite_ref-margaretjane_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-margaretjane-137">[137]</a></sup></p><p>In 2008, PayPal Europe was granted a Luxembourg banking license, which, under European Union law, allows it to conduct banking business throughout the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> It is therefore regulated as a bank by Luxembourg's banking supervisory authority, the Commission de Surveillance du Secteur Financier (CSSF).<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> All of the company's European accounts were transferred to PayPal's bank in Luxembourg in July 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> Prior to this move, PayPal had been registered in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> as PayPal (Europe) Ltd, an entity which was licensed as an Electronic Money Issuer with the UK's <a href="/wiki/Financial_Services_Authority" title="Financial Services Authority">Financial Services Authority</a> (FSA) from 2004. This ceased in 2007, when the company moved to Luxembourg.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p><p>In <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, as of January 2010, PayPal has no cross-border money transfer authorization. In The New York Times article "India's Central Bank Stops Some PayPal Services", Reserve Bank of India spokesman Alpana Killawalla stated: "Providers of cross-border money transfer service need prior authorization from the Reserve Bank under the Payment and Settlement Systems Act, PayPal does not have our authorization."<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> PayPal is not listed in the "Certificates of Authorisation issued by the Reserve Bank of India under the Payment and Settlement Systems Act, 2007 for Setting up and Operating Payment System in India".<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup>
PaisaPay is an Indian sister service to PayPal, and is also owned by eBay.<sup id="cite_ref-paisapay_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-paisapay-146">[146]</a></sup> PaisaPay makes possible payments from abroad by PayPal account holders to Indian sellers on eBay.in.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, PayPal is licensed as an <a href="/wiki/Authorised_deposit-taking_institution" title="Authorised deposit-taking institution">authorised deposit-taking institution</a> (ADI) and is thus subject to Australian banking laws and regulations.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></p><p>In Singapore, PayPal is the holder of a stored value facility that does not require the approval of the <a href="/wiki/Monetary_Authority_of_Singapore" title="Monetary Authority of Singapore">Monetary Authority of Singapore</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(7)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Safety_and_protection_policies">Safety and protection policies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Safety and protection policies" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-7 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-7">
<p>The PayPal Buyer Protection Policy states that the customer may file a buyer complaint if he or she did not receive an item or if the item he or she purchased was significantly not as described. The customer can open a dispute within 180 days (for registered UK residents 180 days, changed 14 June 2014) from the date of payment and escalate it to a claim within 20 days from opening the dispute.  If the buyer used a credit card, he or she might get a refund via <a href="/wiki/Chargeback" title="Chargeback">chargeback</a> from his or her credit-card company. However, in the UK, where such a purchaser is entitled to specific statutory protections (that the credit card company is a second party to the purchase and is therefore equally liable in law if the other party defaults or goes into liquidation) under Section 75 Consumer Credit Act 1979, the purchaser loses this legal protection if the card payment is processed via PayPal.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></p><p>Also, the Financial Ombudsman Service position is that section 75 protection does not apply where PayPal or any eMoney service becomes involved in the credit card transaction. This leaves consumers with no recourse to pursue their complaint with the Financial Ombudsman Service. They only have recourse with the courts. However, the key issues which determine the applicability of section 75 are identified very clearly in Office of Fair Trading v Lloyds TSB Bank Plc and others [2006] EWCA Civ 268 7 and the Bank of Scotland v Alfred Truman (a firm) [2005] [EWHC] 583 (QB). This is a legal authority that section 75 protection does exist where one has paid on a credit card for a product, via an eMoney service.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p><p>According to PayPal, it protects sellers in a limited fashion via the Seller Protection Policy. In general, the Seller Protection Policy is intended to protect the seller from certain kinds of chargebacks or complaints if the seller meets certain conditions including proof of delivery to the buyer. PayPal states the Seller Protection Policy is "designed to protect sellers against claims by buyers of unauthorized payments and against claims of non-receipt of any merchandise". The policy includes a list of "Exclusions" which itself includes "Intangible goods", "Claims for receipt of goods 'not as described<span style="padding-right:.15em;">'</span>", and "Total reversals over the annual limit".<sup id="cite_ref-ppsafety_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ppsafety-151">[151]</a></sup> There are also other restrictions in terms of the sale itself, the payment method and the destination country the item is shipped to (simply having a tracking mechanism is not sufficient to guarantee the Seller Protection Policy is in effect). The PayPal Seller Protection Policy does not provide the additional consumer protection afforded by UK consumer legislation (e.g., Sale of Goods Act) and in addition, it cannot be enforced in the Courts because PayPal operates from Luxembourg, outside all three of the UK legal jurisdictions.<sup id="cite_ref-ppagreement_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ppagreement-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(8)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Security">Security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Security" data-section="26" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-8 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-8">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Security_token">Security token</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Security token" data-section="27" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Security_token" title="Security token">Security token</a></div>
<p>In early 2006, PayPal introduced an optional <a href="/wiki/Security_token" title="Security token">security key</a> as an additional precaution against fraud.<sup id="cite_ref-forbessecurity_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbessecurity-153">[153]</a></sup> A user account tied to a security key has a modified login process. Account-holders enter their login ID and password as normal but are then prompted to enter a six-digit code provided by a credit card sized hardware security key or a text message sent to the account holder's mobile phone. For convenience, users may append the code generated by the hardware key to their password in the login screen. This way they are not prompted for it on another page. This method is required for some services, such as when using PayPal through the eBay application on iPhone.
</p><p>This <a href="/wiki/Two-factor_authentication" class="mw-redirect" title="Two-factor authentication">two-factor authentication</a> is intended to make it difficult for an account to be compromised by a malicious third party without access to the physical security key, although it does not prevent the so-called <a href="/wiki/Man_in_the_Browser" class="mw-redirect" title="Man in the Browser">Man in the Browser</a> (MITB) attacks. However, the user (or malicious third party) can alternatively authenticate by providing the credit card or bank account number listed on their account. Thus the PayPal implementation does not offer the security of true two-factor authentication.<sup id="cite_ref-techhivepp_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-techhivepp-154">[154]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="MTAN">MTAN</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: MTAN" data-section="28" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>It is also possible to use a mobile phone to receive an <a href="/wiki/MTAN" class="mw-redirect" title="MTAN">mTAN</a> (Mobile Transaction Authentication Number) via SMS.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> Use of a security code that is sent to the account holder's mobile phone is currently free.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(9)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Fraud">Fraud</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Fraud" data-section="29" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-9 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-9">
<p>As early as 2001, PayPal had substantial problems with <a href="/wiki/Online_fraud" class="mw-redirect" title="Online fraud">online fraud</a>, especially international hackers who were hacking into PayPal accounts and transferring small amounts of money out of multiple accounts. Standard solutions for merchant and banking fraud might use government criminal sanctions to pursue the fraudsters. But with PayPal losing millions of dollars each month to fraud while experiencing difficulties with using the <a href="/wiki/FBI" class="mw-redirect" title="FBI">FBI</a> to pursue cases of international fraud, PayPal developed a private solution: a "fraud monitoring system that used artificial intelligence to detect potentially fraudulent transactions.  ... Rather than treating the problem of fraud as a <a href="/wiki/Legal_matter_management" title="Legal matter management">legal problem</a>, the company treated it as a <a href="/wiki/Risk_management" title="Risk management">risk management</a> one."<sup id="cite_ref-stringham2013_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stringham2013-157">[157]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="150.2C000_PayPal_cards_frozen"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="150,000_PayPal_cards_frozen">150,000 PayPal cards frozen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: 150,000 PayPal cards frozen" data-section="30" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2015, 150,000 Spanish card holders had their funds frozen in an apparent fraud case involving a PayPal service provider, Younique Money, which was the de facto administrator of the cards. Previously, PayPal had charged €15 to all its card users without authorization (150,000 users). As of March 2015 most funds had not been returned.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(10)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Criticism" data-section="31" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-10 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-10">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_eBay" title="Criticism of eBay">Criticism of eBay</a></div>
<p>In 2003, PayPal voluntarily ceased serving as a payment intermediary between gambling websites and their online customers. At the time of this cessation, it was the largest payment processor for online gambling transactions. In 2010, PayPal resumed accepting such transactions, but only in those countries where online gambling is legal, and only for sites which are properly licensed to operate in said jurisdictions.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup></p><p>If an account is subject to fraud or unauthorized use, PayPal puts the "Limited Access" designation on the account. PayPal has had several notable cases in which the company has frozen the account of users such as Richard Kyanka, owner of the website <a href="/wiki/Something_Awful" title="Something Awful">Something Awful</a>, in September 2005,<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cryptome" title="Cryptome">Cryptome</a> in March 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> or <a href="/wiki/April_Winchell" title="April Winchell">April Winchell</a>, the owner of Regretsy, in December 2011. The account was reinstated, and PayPal apologized and donated to her cause.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2010, PayPal froze the account of a <a href="/wiki/Minecraft" title="Minecraft">Minecraft</a> developer, <a href="/wiki/Markus_Persson" title="Markus Persson">Markus Persson</a>. Persson stated publicly that he had not received a clear explanation of why the account was frozen, and that PayPal was threatening to keep the money if they found anything wrong. His account contained around €600,000.<sup id="cite_ref-rock-paper-shotgun_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rock-paper-shotgun-168">[168]</a></sup></p><p>PayPal's partner <a href="/wiki/MasterCard" class="mw-redirect" title="MasterCard">MasterCard</a> ceased taking donations to <a href="/wiki/WikiLeaks" title="WikiLeaks">WikiLeaks</a> in 2010, and PayPal also suspended, and later permanently restricted, payments to the website after the U.S. State Department deemed WikiLeaks activities as illegal. Online supporters and activists retaliated by subjecting PayPal and MasterCard, along with other companies, to coordinated <a href="/wiki/Cyberattack" title="Cyberattack">cyber attacks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup></p><p>In February 2011 PayPal <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/unbanned" class="extiw" title="wikt:unbanned">unbanned</a> the account of a website that supports <a href="/wiki/List_of_Iraq_War_resisters" title="List of Iraq War resisters">Iraq War resisters</a> after it had enough information to fulfill its <a href="/wiki/Know_your_customer" title="Know your customer">know your customer</a> guidelines. The <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_Manning" title="Chelsea Manning">Chelsea Manning</a> Support Network claimed the backdown was a reaction to a petition to the company to reinstate the account.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2013, PayPal declined to pay a reward offered in its Bug Bounty Program<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> to a 17-year-old German student who had reported a <a href="/wiki/Cross-site_scripting" title="Cross-site scripting">cross-site scripting</a> flaw on its site.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> The company wrote that the vulnerability had been previously reported, and chastised the youth for disclosing the issue to the public, but, uniquely, sent him a "Letter of recognition" for the discovery.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup></p><p>In August 2013, entrepreneurs who had used PayPal to collect the funds they raised on <a href="/wiki/Crowdfunding" title="Crowdfunding">crowdfunding</a> platforms like <a href="/wiki/Kickstarter" title="Kickstarter">Kickstarter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indiegogo" title="Indiegogo">Indiegogo</a> reported difficulty in being able to withdraw the money. Most notable victims are <a href="/wiki/Ouya" title="Ouya">Ouya</a>, GlassUp (a rival to <a href="/wiki/Google_Glass" title="Google Glass">Google Glass</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Mailpile" title="Mailpile">Mailpile</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2014 PayPal blocked the account of a Russian human rights organisation "RosUznik", which supported political prisoners arrested at <a href="/wiki/Bolotnaya_Square_case" title="Bolotnaya Square case">Bolotnaya Square case</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup></p><p>As of January 2015, a class-action lawsuit against PayPal has been filed in <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-178">[178]</a></sup> claiming that they arbitrarily freeze accounts and hold funds for up to 180 days without paying interest and thereby directly profit from it. The lawsuit requests that PayPal be declared a monopoly and thus regulated accordingly.
</p><p>In April 2015 <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> reported PayPal blocking the account of <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>-based human rights group <a href="/wiki/Justice_for_Iran" title="Justice for Iran">Justice for Iran</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2015 PayPal blocked an account intended to raise money for the distribution of <a href="/wiki/Boris_Nemtsov" title="Boris Nemtsov">Boris Nemtsov</a>'s report "<a href="/wiki/Putin._War" title="Putin. War">Putin. War</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> The explanation by PayPal was that "PayPal does not offer the opportunity to use its system for collecting funds to finance the activities of political parties or for political aims in Russia", though PayPal's Acceptable Use Policy does not mention financing for political goals.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> Non-governmental organization <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> issued a statement that "PayPal should immediately lift this ban, to help, rather than hinder, press freedom in Russia."<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup></p><p>By 2016, <a href="/wiki/ConsumerAffairs" title="ConsumerAffairs">ConsumerAffairs</a> had received over 1,200 consumer complaints relating to PayPal policies.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The page cited no longer contains complaints, but only reviews (both positive and negative). (July 2019)">failed verification</span></a></i>]</sup> Consumers have also launched numerous anti-PayPal Facebook sites and Twitter accounts to air their complaints.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup></p><p>In February 2017, PayPal froze the account of <a href="/wiki/News_Media_Canada" title="News Media Canada">News Media Canada</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canadian</a> <a href="/wiki/Trade_association" title="Trade association">trade association</a>, in response to a payment from <a href="/wiki/The_Reminder_(Flin_Flon)" title="The Reminder (Flin Flon)">The Reminder</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Flin_Flon,_Manitoba" class="mw-redirect" title="Flin Flon, Manitoba">Flin Flon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manitoba" title="Manitoba">Manitoba</a> <a href="/wiki/Community_journalism" title="Community journalism">community</a> <a href="/wiki/Newspaper" title="Newspaper">newspaper</a>, intended to cover the fee for the Reminder's submission of articles for consideration in a nationwide journalism contest run by News Media Canada, including one discussing <a href="/wiki/Refugees_of_the_Syrian_Civil_War" title="Refugees of the Syrian Civil War">Syrian refugees</a>. PayPal cited <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> regulations as a reason for flagging the transaction between Canadian entities.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2018, PayPal banned radio host <a href="/wiki/Alex_Jones" title="Alex Jones">Alex Jones</a> and his website <i><a href="/wiki/InfoWars" title="InfoWars">InfoWars</a></i>, claiming that his site has content that was hateful and discriminatory against certain religious groups.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup></p><p>PayPal discontinued payments to <a href="/wiki/Pornhub" title="Pornhub">Pornhub</a> models on November 14, 2019,<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> alleging that "Pornhub has made certain business payments through PayPal without seeking our permission".<sup id="cite_ref-Vice_Pornhub_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vice_Pornhub-189">[189]</a></sup> Pornhub criticized the decision as one that affected "over a hundred thousand performers who rely on them for their livelihoods", and steered its payees toward other payment options.<sup id="cite_ref-Vice_Pornhub_189-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vice_Pornhub-189">[189]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(11)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Litigation">Litigation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Litigation" data-section="32" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-11 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-11">
<p>In March 2002, two PayPal account holders separately sued the company for alleged violations of the Electronic Funds Transfer Act (EFTA) and California law. Most of the allegations concerned PayPal's dispute resolution procedures. The two lawsuits were merged into one class-action lawsuit (In re: PayPal litigation). An informal settlement was reached in November 2003, and a formal settlement was signed on June 11, 2004. The settlement requires that PayPal change its business practices (including changing its dispute resolution procedures to make them EFTA-compliant), as well as making a US$9.25 million payment to members of the class. PayPal denied any wrongdoing.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup></p><p>In June 2003, <a href="/wiki/Stamps.com" title="Stamps.com">Stamps.com</a> filed a lawsuit against PayPal and eBay claiming breach of contract, breach of the implied covenants of good faith and fair dealing, and interference with contract, among other claims. In a 2002 license agreement, Stamps.com and PayPal agreed that Stamps.com technology would be made available to allow PayPal users to buy and print postage online from their PayPal accounts. Stamps.com claimed that PayPal did not live up to its contractual obligations and accused eBay of interfering with PayPal and Stamps.com's agreement, hence Stamp.com's reasoning for including eBay in the suit.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimesarchive_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimesarchive-192">[192]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup></p><p>Craig Comb and two others filed a class action against PayPal in <i>Craig Comb, et al. v. PayPal Inc.</i>. They sued, alleging illegal misappropriation of customer accounts and detailed their customer service experiences, including freezing deposited funds for up to 180 days until disputes were resolved by PayPal. PayPal argued that the plaintiffs were required to arbitrate their disputes under the <a href="/wiki/American_Arbitration_Association" title="American Arbitration Association">American Arbitration Association</a>'s Commercial Arbitration Rules. The court ruled against PayPal, stating that "the User Agreement and arbitration clause are substantively unconscionable under California law."<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2002, <a href="/wiki/Bank_One_Corporation" title="Bank One Corporation">Bank One Corporation</a> sued PayPal for allegedly infringing its cardless payment system patents.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> The following year, PayPal countersued, claiming that Bank One's online bill-payment system was an infringement against PayPal's online bill-payment patent, issued in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> The two companies agreed on a <a href="/wiki/Settlement_(litigation)" title="Settlement (litigation)">settlement</a> in October 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup></p><p>In November 2003, <a href="/wiki/AT%26T_Corporation" title="AT&amp;T Corporation">AT&amp;T Corporation</a> filed suit against eBay and PayPal claiming that their payment systems infringed an AT&amp;T patent, filed in 1991 and granted in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> The case was settled out of court the following month, with the terms of the settlement undisclosed.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup></p><p>In June 2011, PayPal and Israel Credit Cards-Cal Ltd. were sued for <a href="/wiki/New_Israeli_Shekel" class="mw-redirect" title="New Israeli Shekel">NIS</a> 16 million. The claimants accused PayPal of deliberately failing to notify its customers that ICC-Cal was illegally charging them for currency conversion fees.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup></p><p>A class-action lawsuit filed in 2010 was settled in 2016, in which the plaintiffs contested PayPal's "holds" on funds. PayPal has proposed a settlement in the amount of $3.2 million in Zepeda v. PayPal which has yet to be ratified. As part of the settlement, the company agreed to change some of its policies.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="CFPB_consent">CFPB consent</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: CFPB consent" data-section="33" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On 21 May 2015 PayPal agreed that PayPal Credit would pay a $25 million fine to settle a complaint filed in Federal Court by the <a href="/wiki/Consumer_Financial_Protection_Bureau" title="Consumer Financial Protection Bureau">Consumer Financial Protection Bureau</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cfpb_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfpb-100">[100]</a></sup> The complaint alleged that consumers using PayPal were signed up for PayPal credit accounts without their knowledge nor consent. It alleged that PayPal had promised discounts and payment options the consumers never received, and that users trying to sign up for the regular, non-credit, PayPal accounts were signed up for credit accounts instead.<sup id="cite_ref-cfpb_100-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfpb-100">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wp_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wp-202">[202]</a></sup> The complaint was filed in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_District_of_Maryland" title="United States District Court for the District of Maryland">United States District Court for the District of Maryland</a>, which ordered PayPal Credit to refund $15 million to consumers and to pay a $10 million fine.<sup id="cite_ref-cfpb_100-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfpb-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(12)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: See also" data-section="34" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-12 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-12">

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(13)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=PayPal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: References" data-section="35" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-13 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-13">
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">

<li id="cite_note-201"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-201">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ecommercebytes.com/cab/abn/y16/m01/i15/s03">PayPal Agrees to Change Business Practices in Lawsuit Settlement </a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-wp-202"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-wp_202-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Marte, Jonnelle (May 19, 2015). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/get-there/wp/2015/05/19/agency-wants-to-fine-paypal-25-million-to-settle-credit-allegations/">"CFPB seeks to fine PayPal $25 million over credit allegations"</a>. <i>The Washington Post</i><span class="reference-accessdate">.
